The game is known in several countries under different names.\r\nPlayers alternate turns placing a stone of their color on an empty intersection. The name \"Gomoku\" is from the Japanese language, in which it is referred to as gomokunarabe (‰∫îÁõÆ‰∏¶„Åπ). Go means five, moku is a counter word for pieces and narabe means line-up. The game is also popular in Korea, where it is called omok (Ïò§Î™© [‰∫îÁõÆ]) which has the same structure and origin as the Japanese name.\r\nThe Japanese call this game Go-moku (five stones).
